The public was invited to view the project, Grafik Intervention Bryan, which consisted of displays on the Parker Lumber, Kimbell Feed, City National Bank and Ice House buildings. The project was part of Art Step First Friday, which features art, music, horse-drawn carriage rides and other activities in historic downtown Bryan. Originally conceived as a Master of Fine Art graphic design thesis project at the Academy of Art University in San Francisco, Grafik Intervention projects have taken place in several U.S. cities, including San Marcos, Texas. The projections are designed to provide historical information and to inspire community members to consider the potential of currently unused buildings.  \u201cThe design students\u2019 extensive research in compiling historical information to create the projections involved contacting the buildings\u2019 previous owners, visiting the Carnegie History Center, Bryan Public Library, Texas A&M\u2019s Cushing and Evans Libraries, contacting former employees and longtime Bryan citizens, and meeting with representatives of the city of Bryan,\u201d said Donna Hajash, senior lecturer of visualization, who is leading the studio.Cast: TAMU College of ArchitectureTags:  Texas A&M,  Grafik Intervention,  Donna Hajash  and Texas A&M Department of Visualiz"}

Working toward a strict deadline, every team completed their project and then had the honor of their work being showcased at the international computer-graphics conference known as SIGGRAPH. students\u2019 projects, juried by a group of design professionals, were previously selected by department faculty as the academic year\u2019s top graduate study projects.\n\nOther graduate student award recipients were: Peri Arthur, presented with the Henry Adams Certificate; Akshay Sangolli, presented with the Henry Adams Medal; Amy Kircher, presented with the Alpha Rho Chi Medal and Pasquale de Paola, presented with the Architectural Research Centers Consortium\u2019s King Medal. \n\nUndergraduate students recognized with top integrated studio projects were Marquesa Figueroa, Troy Grant, senior architecture lecturer, were announced as recipients of graduate and undergraduate teaching awards, respectively, after a student vote.\n\n\u201cThese awards recognize not only our most promising students and their individual accomplishments, but also represent the level of excellence of all our students,\u201d said Ward Wells, head of the Department of Architecture. \u201cThe ", "id": "10150796536210420_22979372", "user_likes": false}]}, "actions": [{"link": "https://www.facebook.com/11950375419/posts/10150796541940420", "name": "Comment"}, {"link": "https://www.facebook.com/11950375419/posts/10150796541940420", "name": "Like"}], "updated_time": "2013-04-17T07:08:23+0000", "caption": "Paolo Barucchieri, affiliated with Texas A&M\u2019s study abroad program in Italy since 1982, has died after a battle with cancer.\n\nIn addition to his duties as founding director of the Santa Chiara Study Center in Castiglion Fiorentino, Barucchieri was also an executive professor, whose subjects included design theory, Italian medieval and Renaissance art history and design/mixed-media studio. He also led students on field trips and study tours.\n\n\u201cDespite his heroic fight and the unrelenting care of the doctors in Rome, the progress of this cancer could not be stopped,\u201d said his wife, Sharon. \u201cPaolo\u2019s strength and dignity throughout this horrific period was nothing less than inspiring. The extreme pain and complete lack of mobility for months was very hard on him, but he never gave up hope. From his bedside he attended to program details and worried about the students having a good experience.\u201d\n\nHe slowly lost his voice during the ordeal, said his wife, but he kept his sense of humor right up to the end, joked with nurses insisted they learn some Tuscan expressions and quizzed them on art history. \n\nBarucchieri earned a Ph.D. in Italian medieval art in 1972, a Master of Fine Art at the University of Northern Colorado in 1969 and a Bachelor of Art in Architectural Design at the University of Florence, Italy in 1967. \n\nHe brought his first group of students to Italy in 1972 as a faculty member at the University of Northern Colorado, where they stayed at a monastery. He founded Santa Chiara in 1989 with Texas A&M as its founding institute. \n\n'It will not be easy to move forward without him; his insight and guidance and the beautiful way he shared Italy without exclusion of anyone gave the program its heart, said Sharon. \u201cThe world without our Captain Paolo is a different place; it seems emptier, more quiet, less interesting.\u201d \n\nAlso see \"Remembering Paolo\" Facebook group:\nhttp://www.facebook.com/groups/241558545941610/ ", "link": "https://www.facebook.com/photo.php?fbid=10150796536310420&set=a.10150796536210420.473626.11950375419&type=1&relevant_count=4", "object_id": "10150796536310420", "shares": {"count": 54}, "created_time": "2012-04-09T20:57:51+0000", "message": "Paolo Barucchieri, affiliated with Texas A&M\u2019s study abroad program in Italy since 1982, has died after a battle with cancer.\n\nIn addition to his duties as founding director of the Santa Chiara Study Center in Castiglion Fiorentino, Barucchieri was also an executive professor, whose subjects included design theory, Italian medieval and Renaissance art history and design/mixed-media studio. He also led students on field trips and study tours.\n\n\u201cDespite his heroic fight and the unrelenting care of the doctors in Rome, the progress of this cancer could not be stopped,\u201d said his wife, Sharon. \u201cPaolo\u2019s strength and dignity throughout this horrific period was nothing less than inspiring. The extreme pain and complete lack of mobility for months was very hard on him, but he never gave up hope. From his bedside he attended to program details and worried about the students having a good experience.\u201d\n\nHe slowly lost his voice during the ordeal, said his wife, but he kept his sense of humor right up to the end, joked with nurses insisted they learn some Tuscan expressions and quizzed them on art history. \n\nBarucchieri earned a Ph.D. in Italian medieval art in 1972, a Master of Fine Art at the University of Northern Colorado in 1969 and a Bachelor of Art in Architectural Design at the University of Florence, Italy in 1967. \n\nHe brought his first group of students to Italy in 1972 as a faculty member at the University of Northern Colorado, where they stayed at a monastery. He founded Santa Chiara in 1989 with Texas A&M as its founding institute. \n\n'It will not be easy to move forward without him; his insight and guidance and the beautiful way he shared Italy without exclusion of anyone gave the program its heart, said Sharon. \u201cThe world without our Captain Paolo is a different place; it seems emptier, more quiet, less interesting.\u201d \n\nAlso see \"Remembering Paolo\" Facebook group:\nhttp://www.facebook.com/groups/241558545941610/ ", "type": "photo", "id": "11950375419_10150796541940420", "status_type": "added_photos", "icon": "https://fbstatic-a.akamaihd.net/rsrc.php/v2/yz/r/StEh3RhPvjk.gif"}

Melnick, professor of landscape architecture and director of the John Yeon Center for Architectural Studies at the University of Oregon, presents \"Protecting Resources That Matter in a Future of Uncertainty,\" the keynote address of \u201cDisaster,\u201d the 13th Annual Historic Preservation symposium at Texas A&M. The event was sponsored by the Center for Heritage Conservation and the Hazard Reduction & Recovery Center Feb. 24 - 25, 2012. Melnick discussed the future of cultural resource protection in light of critical environmental and social developments, with special attention to unanticipated disasters.  As an internationally recognized expert in cultural landscape evaluation and historic landscape preservation planning, he suggested reconsidering how critical cultural resources are identified. He focused on the need for stability and flexibility in approaches to preservation, identify lessons from other fields and propose future preservation strategies. For more about the 2012 symposium, visit one.arch.tamu.edu/news/2012/1/19/disaster-symposium/.Cast: TAMU College of ArchitectureTags:  Texas A&M,  Robert Z. Melnick,  Center for Heritage Conservation,  Hazard Reduction & Recovery  and Historic Preservation Symposium"}

Working at his drafting table, surrounded by his fellow students, they added, will be among the happiest memories of his life.  \n\n\u201cBobby was following his lifelong dream of becoming an architect,\u201d they said. \u201cWe hope that you too will follow your dreams, both in your architecture studies and in life.
